      <p>
       This is a
       <b>
        list of solar eclipses in the 6th century BC
       </b>
       . During the period 600 to 501 BC there were 255
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse" title="Solar eclipse">
        solar eclipses
       </a>
       of which 96 were partial, 86 were annular (one
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse#Terminology" title="Solar eclipse">
        non-central
       </a>
       ), 65 were total, and 8 were hybrids. The greatest number of eclipses in one year was five, in 569 and 504 BC, and three months, September 591 BC, August 515 BC, and July 504 BC, had two eclipses.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa_catalog_list_1-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nasa_catalog_list-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The solar eclipse of May 28, 585 BC that ended the
       <a href="/wiki/Eclipse_of_Thales" title="Eclipse of Thales">
        Battle of Halys
       </a>
       has made this battle the earliest historical event the date of which is exactly known.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
